SAN JUAN TEACHERS ASSOCIATION
Online Learning Educational Options Prototype

Background

Each year in San Juan Unified School District (SJUSD) many students drop out from our traditional high
schools or graduate without meeting the minimum requirements for California state university system
admission. Most exit, or lack admission requirements, because they are credit deficient or lack the
acceptable GPA. Currently the San Juan Unified School District provides very limited opportunities for
students to recapture credits or improve their GPA prior to their graduation and/or college application.

Intent:

The intent of this prototype is to target students who would otherwise be disenfranchised at a
comprehensive high school and provide alternative services for re-engagement at the comprehensive site.
The prototype will have two levels of support:

1.    Credit recovery at the comprehensive sites (in 2013-14 SJUSD processed more than 2,800
applications for credit recovery or missing courses; most times the classes were held outside of the
students’ high school campus)

2.    Create an additional system of support for students at their high school for academic growth and
success

More specifically the intent of this prototype is to target students who:

1.    Have failed semester or full year classes to recapture credits

2.    Have a need to retake a SJUSD ‘a-g’ course for grade improvement

This prototype is not intended to replace initial classroom-based instruction and students will need to
apply for this prototype, as participation is voluntary. School staff will identify the students who could
benefit from this program and students will be accepted based on space and the following priority list:

1.    Current 12th grade student who needs additional 10 or less credits to graduate in addition to full
student load

2.    Current 12th grade student who needs 10 or less credits for grade improvement to qualify for ‘a-g’
requirements

3.    Current 12th grade student who is credit deficient and not on track to graduate, who needs 11 or
more credits to graduate in addition to full student load

4.    Current 11* grade student who is credit deficient and not on track to graduate and/or who has
failed a core class

5.    Current 11* grade student who needs 10 or less credits for grade improvement to qualify for ‘a-g’
requirements

6.    Incoming 10th grade student who is credit deficient and not on track to graduate and/or who has
failed a core class

Agreement

The San Juan Unified School District and the San Juan Teachers Association hereby agree to the
following provisions regarding the after-school or before-school Online Learning Educational Options 195

SJTA 14-16

Prototype at: Bella Vista, Casa Roble, Del Campo, El Camino, Encina, Mesa Verde, Mira Loma, San

Memorandum of Understanding
Between the
San Juan Unified School District
And

The San Juan Teachers Association
System of Professional Growth Prototype

Background

The purpose of this Memorandum of Understanding is to implement the next phase of
the work outlined in the collective bargaining agreement (Exhibit N-l) regarding the
Joint Committee's Work on Teacher Evaluation. Specifically, the statement of intent in
Exhibit N-l specifies the following vision for such work:

It is the deeply held belief of both SJTA and SJUSD that educators are
professionals that continue to grow and improve in their craft throughout their
career. All levels of experience and effectiveness deserve an environment in
which to further their skills. The current model of evaluations does little to
support this belief.

Interests

Therefore, it is the interest of both SJUSD and SJTA to create a systematic, non-
adversarial process that supports all teachers in their ongoing professional growth. This
new prototype could change the structure of what we now refer to as "evaluation." This
new prototype sees the teacher as a key participant, and will be practitioner-driven.

The focus of this work is to benefit the whole, through collaboration, shared practice,
and the deprivatization of the profession.

Provisions of the MOU

Therefore the parties hereby agree to the following provisions regarding the
development of the prototype, hereafter identified as the "System of Professional
Growth Prototype" (SPGP), during the 2014-2015 school year. The purpose of
prototyping is to give form to an idea to learn about strengths and weaknesses of the
prototypes and to identify new directions for the next phase of developing a pilot.

1) The Joint Committee on Teacher Evaluation shall be identified as the Professional
Growth Team and shall oversee the SPGP and the implementation of the prototype
described in Attachment A. The President of SJTA and the Superintendent's designee
shall chair this team. The work of this team shall include: coordination with the

SJTA 14-16

197

researchers Julie Koppich and Daniel Humphrey (who will document the strengths and
weaknesses of our professional growth prototype), budget oversight, establishing the
selection process of teachers and administrators who wish to volunteer during this
prototype, designing and establishing the calibration training, selecting the participants,
addressing issues that may arise during the prototype year, and providing scheduled
updates to the District and SJTA at least twice during the 2014-2015 school year.

2)    The budget for 2014-2015 year of prototyping shall be no more than $150,000.00

3)    The Professional Growth Team shall follow the established criteria for individual
participation (see Attachment B).

4)    Members who volunteer to serve as participants or observers in the prototyping
process shall be held harmless. Our goal is to test the prototype, not the person, so
outcomes that are a result of the prototype will be used to inform the process only.

5)    Due to the additional work required in trainings, focus groups, and increased
workload, teachers selected as program participants shall be paid a stipend as follows:

a.    "Participants" (teachers who volunteer to be observed; not to exceed 60):

d.    Consulting Teachers (who volunteer to create and deliver training, not to
exceed eight in number); $1,500.00 per participant (up to a maximum of $12,000.00 for
all participants)

6)    The application and selection process shall be completed no later than June 5, 2014.

2015 school year except for those required to be evaluated under Education Code and

•    Members participating in the Peer Assistant Review Program per §3.08 and

3.09

•    Members with 10 or more years of employment who are notified no later than
June 30 by Human Resources for evaluation

term of this agreement.

Essential Elements:

The following identified elements of the California Teaching Standards have
been determined by the New Teacher Center to have the greatest impact on

student learning:

Standard 1. Engaging and supporting all students in learning

1.5 Promoting critical thinking through inquiry, problem solving, and reflection.

As teachers develop, they may ask, "How do I..." or "Why do I...”

•    encourage students to use multiple approaches and solutions to solve
problems?

•    encourage students to ask critical questions and consider diverse perspectives
about subject matter?

•    provide opportunities for students to think about, discuss, and evaluate
content?

•    ask questions to facilitate discussion, clarify, and extend students' thinking?

•    support students to think and communicate with clarity and precision?

•    help students apply previous learning to new situations?

•    encourage students to create, imagine, and innovate?

•    help students to develop and use strategies and technologies for accessing
knowledge and information?

•    Observation/Video

•    Student work (journals, goals, etc.)

•    Feedback to students and impact on stu dent learning

SIDE LETTER OF AGREEMENT

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT (District)

and the

SAN JUAN TEACHERS ASSOCIATION (Association)

Regarding the Early Childhood Education 2014-2015 Salary Schedule Migration

Background;

The District and SJTA are committed to working together to ensure strong ECE programs and
services for children and families, wherein all teachers and staff are effectively supported and
appropriately compensated to provide this high level of service.

On May of 2012, the District and SJTA agreed upon a seven (7) year ECE Salary
Schedule migration towards a consolidated salary schedule. At the time, both parties
recognized that because of the uncertainty of funding, the scale, and the extended
timeline, the salary schedule migration might require adjustments. Therefore, the parties
agreed to convene the Budget Review Committee (BRC) annually to determine the
feasibility of percentages and make recommendations for the full range of options.

In recent years, the lack of state and federal funding for early childhood education has had an
impact on the ECE Department's ability to remain fiscally solvent. Recent shifts in state funding
include a 5% standard reimbursement rate increase for State Preschool. While this is helpful, it
positively affects less than 15% of our overall ECE budget.

Intent:

The intent of this Side Letter of Agreement between the District and the Association is to modify
the ECE Salary Schedule migration for the 2014-2015 school year.

Agreement:

The District and the Association hereby agree that instead of the scheduled ECE Salary Schedule
migration from 37% to 52%, the migration will be 37% to 43.25% for 2014-2015.

This Side Letter of Agreement is non-precedential and is for the 2014-15 school year. The
parties shall continue to review annually the feasibility of the timeline per the collective
bargaining agreement and absent any other adjustment, the original rate of implementation shall
be in effect in 2015-16.

On Behalf of^San Juan Unified School District

Jim Shqemake    Date

San Juan Unified School District

On Behalf of San Juan Teachers Association
